<p><b>North America</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> entirely within the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> and almost all within the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>. It can also be considered a northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">subcontinent</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-northamerica_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-northamerica-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> It is bordered to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, to the west and south by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, and to the southeast by <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.</p>
<p>North America covers an area of about 24,709,000 square kilometers (9,540,000 square miles), about 16.5% of the earth's land area and about 4.8% of its total surface. North America is the third largest continent by area, following <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_continents_by_population" title="List of continents by population">fourth</a> by population after Asia, Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, its population was estimated at nearly 565 million people in <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_North_America" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America">23 independent states</a>, or about 7.5% of the world's population, if nearby islands (most notably the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>) are included.</p>
<p>North America was reached by its <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">first human populations</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, via crossing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bering_land_bridge" title="Bering land bridge">Bering land bridge</a>. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleo-Indian</a> period is taken to have lasted until about 10,000 years ago (the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Archaic_period_in_North_America" title="Archaic period in North America">Archaic or Meso-Indian</a> period). The <a href="/wiki/Classic_stage" title="Classic stage">Classic stage</a> spans roughly the 6th to 13th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a> ended with the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_migrations" title="Transatlantic migrations">transatlantic migrations</a> and the arrival of European settlers during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_period" title="Early Modern period">Early Modern period</a>. Present-day cultural and ethnic patterns reflect different kind of interactions between <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> and their descendants. European influences are strongest in the northern parts of the continent while indigenous and African influences are relatively stronger in the south. Because of the history of colonialism, most North Americans speak English, Spanish or French and societies and states commonly reflect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_civilization" title="Western civilization">Western traditions</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<p><span id="Etymology"></span></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="314" data-file-width="400" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg/220px-Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg/330px-Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of North America, from 1621.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">The Americas</a> are usually accepted as having been named after the Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> by the German cartographers <a href="/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller" title="Martin Waldseemüller">Martin Waldseemüller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann" title="Matthias Ringmann">Matthias Ringmann</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> Vespucci, who explored South America between 1497 and 1502, was the first <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> to suggest that the Americas were not the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>, but a different landmass previously unknown by Europeans. In 1507, Waldseemüller produced a world map, in which he placed the word "America" on the continent of South America, in the middle of what is today Brazil. He explained the rationale for the name in the accompanying book <i>Cosmographiae Introductio</i>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p><i><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">... ab Americo inventore ... quasi Americi terram sive Americam</span></i> (from Americus the discoverer ... as if it were the land of Americus, thus America).</p>
</blockquote>
<p>For Waldseemüller, no one should object to the naming of the land after its discoverer. He used the Latinized version of Vespucci's name (Americus Vespucius), but in its feminine form "America", following the examples of "Europa", "Asia" and "Africa".</p>
<p>Later, other mapmakers extended the name <i>America</i> to the northern continent, In 1538, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerard_Mercator" title="Gerard Mercator">Gerard Mercator</a> used <i>America</i> on his map of the world for all the Western Hemisphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some argue that the convention is to use the surname for naming discoveries except in the case of royalty and so a derivation from "Amerigo Vespucci" could be problematic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> Ricardo Palma (1949) proposed a derivation from the "Amerrique" mountains of Central America—Vespucci was the first to discover South America and the <i>Amerrique</i> mountains of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, which connected his discoveries to those of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hudd" title="Alfred Hudd">Alfred E. Hudd</a> proposed a theory in 1908 that the continents are named after a Welsh merchant named <a href="/wiki/Richard_Amerike" title="Richard Amerike">Richard Amerike</a> from Bristol, who is believed to have financed <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a>'s voyage of discovery from England to <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> in 1497. A minutely explored belief that has been advanced is that America was named for a Spanish sailor bearing the ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visigothic" title="Visigothic">Visigothic</a> name of 'Amairick'. Another is that the name is rooted in a <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a> language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent"><span id="Usage_of_the_term">Extent</span></span></h2>
<p>The term <i>North America</i> maintains various definitions in accordance with location and context. In <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">Canadian English</a>, <i>North America</i> may be used to refer to the United States and Canada together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Alternatively, usage sometimes includes <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAGreenland_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIAGreenland-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNotes_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-eNotes-14">[13]</a></sup> and Mexico (as in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilateral_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trilateral-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spp_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-spp-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-epa-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About.com_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-About.com-18">[17]</a></sup> as well as offshore islands. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme_for_the_Americas" title="United Nations geoscheme for the Americas">UN geoscheme</a> for "North America" separates Mexico from the United States and Canada, placing it instead within its designated "Central America" region, while also treating the islands of the Caribbean separately from the US/Canada definition—the UN's "North America" definition still includes the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Arctic_Archipelago" title="Canadian Arctic Archipelago">Canadian Arctic Archipelago</a> and Greenland together with the US/Canada continental definition, with both insular entities being tectonically on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_plate" title="North American plate">North American plate</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and the countries of Latin America, the <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognates</a> of <i>North America</i> usually designate a subcontinent of the Americas comprising Canada, the United States, and Mexico, and often Greenland, Saint Pierre et Miquelon, and Bermuda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>North America has been historically referred to by other names. Spanish North America (<a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>) was often referred to as <i><a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Northern_America_(disambiguation)" title="Northern America (disambiguation)">Northern America</a></i>, and this was the <a href="/wiki/Solemn_Act_of_the_Declaration_of_Independence_of_Northern_America" title="Solemn Act of the Declaration of Independence of Northern America">first official name</a> given to Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AGN_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-AGN-24">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Canada" title="List of regions of Canada">List of regions of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Mexico" title="List of regions of Mexico">List of regions of Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_United_States" title="List of regions of the United States">List of regions of the United States</a></div>
<p>Geographically the North American continent has many regions and subregions. These include cultural, economic, and geographic regions. Economic regions included those formed by trade blocs, such as the North American Trade Agreement bloc and Central American Trade Agreement. Linguistically and culturally, the continent could be divided into <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">Anglo-America</a> and Latin America. Anglo-America includes most of Northern America, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, and Caribbean islands with English-speaking populations (though sub-national entities, such as <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">Francophone</a> in composition).</p>
<p>The southern North American continent is composed of two regions. These are Central America and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaCA_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaCA-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> The north of the continent maintains recognized regions as well. In contrast to the common definition of "North America", that which encompasses the whole continent, the term "North America" is also used to refer to Canada, Mexico, the United States, and Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAGreenland_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAGreenland-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNotes_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-eNotes-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilateral_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trilateral-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term Northern America refers to the northern-most countries and territories of North America, Canada, the United States, Greenland, Bermuda, and St. Pierre and Miquelon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Although rarely used,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> the term <a href="/wiki/Middle_America_(Americas)" title="Middle America (Americas)">Middle America</a>—not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a>—groups the regions of Central America, the Caribbean, and Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest countries of the continent, Canada and the United States, also contain well-defined and recognized regions. In the case of Canada these are the <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_Coast" title="British Columbia Coast">British Columbia Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Prairies" title="Canadian Prairies">Canadian Prairies</a>, Central Canada, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, and Northern Canada. These regions also contain many subregions. In the case of the United States – and in accordance with the US Census Bureau definitions – these regions are: <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Mid-Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_North_Central_States" title="East North Central States">East North Central States</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_North_Central_States" title="West North Central States">West North Central States</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_States" title="South Atlantic States">South Atlantic States</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_South_Central_States" title="East South Central States">East South Central States</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_South_Central_States" title="West South Central States">West South Central States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">Mountain States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_States" title="Pacific States">Pacific States</a>. Regions shared between both nations included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region_(North_America)" title="Great Lakes region (North America)">Great Lakes Region</a>. <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" title="Megalopolis (city type)">Megalopolises</a> have also formed between both nations in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Megaregion" title="Great Lakes Megaregion">Great Lakes Megaregion</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">History of North America</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geologic_history">Geologic history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="900" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png/220px-NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png/330px-NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png/440px-NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NorthAmerica-WaterDivides.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Principal hydrological divides of North America.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Laurentia" title="Laurentia">Laurentia</a> is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">craton</a> which forms the geologic core of North America; it formed between 1.5 and 1.0 billion years ago during the <a href="/wiki/Proterozoic" title="Proterozoic">Proterozoic</a> eon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a> is the largest exposure of this craton. From the Late <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic" title="Paleozoic">Paleozoic</a> to Early <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a> eras, North America was joined with the other modern-day continents as part of the supercontinent <a href="/wiki/Pangaea" title="Pangaea">Pangaea</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> to its east. One of the results of the formation of Pangaea was the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Taconic_orogeny" title="Taconic orogeny">formed</a> some 480 million years ago, making it among the oldest mountain ranges in the world. When Pangaea began to rift around 200 million years ago, North America became part of <a href="/wiki/Laurasia" title="Laurasia">Laurasia</a>, before it separated from Eurasia as its own continent during the mid-<a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-45">[38]</a></sup> The Rockies and other western mountain ranges began forming around this time from a period of mountain building called the <a href="/wiki/Laramide_orogeny" title="Laramide orogeny">Laramide orogeny</a>, between 80 and 55 million years ago. The formation of the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a> that connected the continent to South America arguably occurred approximately 12 to 15 million years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Origins_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Origins-46">[39]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> (as well as many other northern freshwater lakes and rivers) were carved by receding glaciers about 10,000 years ago.</p>
<p>North America is the source of much of what humanity knows about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geologic_time" title="Geologic time">geologic time</a> periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-47">[40]</a></sup> The geographic area that would later become the United States has been the source of more varieties of <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a> than any other modern country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-47">[40]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontologist</a> Peter Dodson, this is primarily due to stratigraphy, climate and geography, human resources, and history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-47">[40]</a></sup> Much of the Mesozoic Era is represented by exposed outcrops in the many arid regions of the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dinopedia-american_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-dinopedia-american-47">[40]</a></sup> The most significant <a href="/wiki/Late_Jurassic" title="Late Jurassic">Late Jurassic</a> dinosaur-bearing fossil deposit in North America is the <a href="/wiki/Morrison_Formation" title="Morrison Formation">Morrison Formation</a> of the western United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jurassicdistribution_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-jurassicdistribution-48">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1,_Mexico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2669" data-file-width="4243" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1%2C_Mexico.jpg/220px-Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1%2C_Mexico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1%2C_Mexico.jpg/330px-Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1%2C_Mexico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1%2C_Mexico.jpg/440px-Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1%2C_Mexico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1,_Mexico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/El_Castillo,_Chichen_Itza" title="El Castillo, Chichen Itza"><i>El Castillo</i></a> pyramid, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1" title="Chichén Itzá">Chichén Itzá</a>, Mexico.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The indigenous peoples of North America have many <a href="/wiki/Creation_myth" title="Creation myth">creation myths</a> by which they assert that they have been present on the land since its creation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtin2014_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curtin2014-49">[42]</a></sup> The specifics of <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">Paleo-Indian migration to and throughout the Americas</a>, including the exact dates and routes traveled, are subject to ongoing research and discussion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White2006_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-White2006-50">[43]</a></sup> The traditional theory has been that these early migrants moved into the <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Beringia land bridge</a> between eastern Siberia and present-day Alaska around 25,000 to 11,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HavilandPrins2013_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-HavilandPrins2013-51">[44]</a></sup> The few agreements achieved to date are the origin from <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, with widespread habitation of the Americas during the end of the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, or more specifically what is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Glacial_Maximum#North_America" title="Late Glacial Maximum">late glacial maximum</a>, around 13,000 years before present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pauketat2012_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pauketat2012-52">[45]</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Genetic history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">genetic research</a> indicated secondary waves of migration occurred after the initial Paleo-Indian colonization,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SkoglundMallick2015_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-SkoglundMallick2015-53">[46]</a></sup> but prior to modern <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inupiat" title="Inupiat">Inupiat</a> and Yupik expansions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BellwoodNess2014_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-BellwoodNess2014-54">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">Before contact with Europeans</a>, the natives of North America were divided into many different polities, from small <a href="/wiki/Band_society" title="Band society">bands</a> of a few families to large empires. They lived in several "<a href="/wiki/Classification_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Classification of indigenous peoples of the Americas">culture areas</a>", which roughly correspond to <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_America" title="Geography of North America">geographic and biological zones</a> and give a good indication of the main <a href="/wiki/Lifeway" title="Lifeway">lifeway</a> or occupation of the people who lived there (e.g., the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plains_Bison" title="Plains Bison">bison</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunters</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plains_Indian" title="Plains Indian">Great Plains</a>, or the farmers of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>). Native groups can also be classified by their <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">language family</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Athabaskan_languages" title="Athabaskan languages">Athapascan</a> or <a href="/wiki/Uto-Aztecan_languages" title="Uto-Aztecan languages">Uto-Aztecan</a>). Peoples with similar languages did not always share the same <a href="/wiki/Material_culture" title="Material culture">material culture</a>, nor were they always <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allies" title="Allies">allies</a>. Anthropologists think that the Inuit people of the high <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> came to North America much later than other native groups, as evidenced by the disappearance of <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset culture</a> artifacts from the <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_record" title="Archaeological record">archaeological record</a>, and their replacement by the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a>.</p>
<p>During the thousands of years of native habitation on the continent, cultures changed and shifted. One of the oldest cultures yet found is the <a href="/wiki/Clovis_culture" title="Clovis culture">Clovis culture</a> of modern <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>. Later cultures include the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> and related <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mound_builder_(people)" title="Mound builder (people)">Mound building</a> cultures, found in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_river" title="Mississippi river">Mississippi river</a> valley and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Pueblo_Peoples" title="Ancient Pueblo Peoples">Pueblo culture</a> of what is now the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners" title="Four Corners">Four Corners</a>. The more southern cultural groups of North America were responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a> of many common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crops" title="Crops">crops</a> now used around the world, such as tomatoes and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squash_(plant)" title="Squash (plant)">squash</a>. Perhaps most importantly they domesticated one of the world's major staples, maize (corn).</p>
<p>The earliest verifiable instance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_trans-oceanic_contact" title="Pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact">pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact</a> by any European culture with the landmasses that geologically constitute the "mainland" of modern North America has been dated to the end of the 10th century CE - this site, situated at the northernmost extent of the island named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, is known as <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L'Anse aux Meadows">L'Anse aux Meadows</a>, where unmistakable evidence of <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> settlement was uncovered in the early 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result of the development of agriculture in the south, many important cultural advances were made there. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya civilization</a> developed a <a href="/wiki/Maya_script" title="Maya script">writing system</a>, built <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_pyramids" title="Mesoamerican pyramids">huge pyramids and temples</a>, had a <a href="/wiki/Maya_calendar" title="Maya calendar">complex calendar</a>, and developed the concept of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/0_(number)" title="0 (number)">zero</a> around 400 CE, a few hundred years after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesopotamians" title="Mesopotamians">Mesopotamians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[49]</a></sup> The Mayan culture was still present in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucatan_Peninsula" title="Yucatan Peninsula">southern Mexico</a> and Guatemala when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadors" title="Conquistadors">Spanish</a> explorers arrived, but political dominance in the area had shifted to the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztec Empire</a> whose capital city <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a> was located further north in the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valley of Mexico</a>. The Aztecs were conquered in 1521 by <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grunberg_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grunberg-57">[50]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_West_005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/220px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/330px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Benjamin_West_005.jpg/440px-Benjamin_West_005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_West_005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Benjamin_West" title="Benjamin West">Benjamin West</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe" title="The Death of General Wolfe">The Death of General Wolfe</a></i> (1771) depicting the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">Battle of the Plains of Abraham</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_European_colonization_of_North_America" title="Timeline of the European colonization of North America">Timeline of the European colonization of North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_America" title="French America">French America</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">Viceroyalty of New Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Russian colonization of the Americas">Russian colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, Europeans explored and staked claims to various parts of North America. Upon their arrival in the "<a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>", the Native American population <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">declined substantially</a>, because of violent conflicts with the invaders and the introduction of European diseases to which the Native Americans lacked immunity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[51]</a></sup> Native culture changed drastically and their affiliation with political and cultural groups also changed. Several linguistic groups <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">died out</a>, and others changed quite quickly. The names and cultures that Europeans recorded were not necessarily the same as the names they had used a few generations before, or the ones in use today.</p>
<p>Britain, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and France took over extensive territories in North America - and fought over them. In the late 18th century and beginning of the 19th, independence movements that sprung up across the continent, led to the creation of the modern countries in the area. The 13 British colonies on the North Atlantic coast declared independence in 1776, becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America">United States of America</a>. Canada was formed from the unification of northern territories controlled by Britain and France. New Spain, a territory that stretched from modern-day southern US to Central America, declared independence in 1810, becoming the <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">First Mexican Empire</a>. In 1823 the former <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">Captaincy General of Guatemala</a>, then part of the Mexican Empire, became the first <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">independent state</a> in Central America, officially changing its name to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">United Provinces of Central America</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography"><span id="Geography_and_extent">Geography</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_America" title="Geography of North America">Geography of North America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1748" data-file-width="1624" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg/220px-North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg/330px-North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg/440px-North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North_America_satellite_orthographic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite imagery of North America.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North America occupies the northern portion of the landmass generally referred to as the New World, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">the Americas</a>, or simply America (which, less commonly, is considered by some as a single <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOC_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-IOC-59">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oceano_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oceano-60">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cincocontinentes_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-cincocontinentes-61">[54]</a></sup> with North America a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">subcontinent</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[55]</a></sup> North America's only land connection to <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> is at the Isthmus of Panama. The continent is delimited on the southeast by most geographers at the <a href="/wiki/Dari%C3%A9n_Gap" title="Darién Gap">Darién watershed</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>-Panama border, placing all of Panama within North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-North_America_Atlas_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-North_America_Atlas-65">[58]</a></sup> Alternatively, some geologists physiographically locate its southern limit at the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">Isthmus of Tehuantepec</a>, Mexico, with Central America extending southeastward to South America from this point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[59]</a></sup> The Caribbean islands, or West Indies, are considered part of North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-northamerica_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-northamerica-3">[2]</a></sup> The continental coastline is long and irregular. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> is the largest body of water indenting the continent, followed by <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a>. Others include the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">Gulf of Saint Lawrence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>.</p>
<p>Before the Central American isthmus formed, the region had been underwater. The islands of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> delineate a submerged former <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a>, which had connected North and South America via what are now <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.</p>
<p>There are numerous islands off the continent's coasts; principally, the Arctic Archipelago, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_%26_Caicos" title="Turks &amp; Caicos">Turks &amp; Caicos</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> (some of which are in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern Hemisphere</a> proper), the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago" title="Alexander Archipelago">Alexander Archipelago</a>, the many thousand islands of the British Columbia Coast, and Newfoundland. Greenland, a self-governing Danish island, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">world's largest</a>, is on the same <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">tectonic plate</a> (the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>) and is part of North America geographically. In a geologic sense, Bermuda is not part of the Americas, but an oceanic island which was formed on the fissure of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a> over 100 million years ago. The nearest landmass to it is <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>. However, Bermuda is often thought of as part of North America, especially given its historical, political and cultural ties to <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> and other parts of the continent.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moraine_Lake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2775" data-file-width="4000" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Moraine_Lake.jpg/220px-Moraine_Lake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Moraine_Lake.jpg/330px-Moraine_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Moraine_Lake.jpg/440px-Moraine_Lake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moraine_Lake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moraine_Lake" title="Moraine Lake">Moraine Lake</a> in <a href="/wiki/Banff_National_Park" title="Banff National Park">Banff National Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The vast majority of North America is on the North American Plate. Parts of western Mexico, including Baja California, and of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, including the cities of <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_California" title="Santa Cruz, California">Santa Cruz</a>, lie on the eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">Pacific Plate</a>, with the two plates meeting along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Andreas_fault" title="San Andreas fault">San Andreas fault</a>. The southernmost portion of the continent and much of the West Indies lie on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Plate" title="Juan de Fuca Plate">Juan de Fuca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocos_Plate" title="Cocos Plate">Cocos plates</a> border the North American Plate on its western frontier.</p>
<p>The continent can be divided into four great regions (each of which contains many subregions): the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> stretching from the Gulf of Mexico to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Canadian Arctic</a>; the geologically young, mountainous west, including the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">Great Basin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_California" title="Geography of California">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>; the raised but relatively flat plateau of the Canadian Shield in the northeast; and the varied eastern region, which includes the Appalachian Mountains, the coastal plain along the Atlantic seaboard, and the Florida peninsula. Mexico, with its long <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_cordillera" title="American cordillera">cordilleras</a>, falls largely in the western region, although the eastern coastal plain does extend south along the Gulf.</p>
<p>The western mountains are split in the middle into the main range of the Rockies and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Ranges" title="Pacific Coast Ranges">coast ranges</a> in California, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, with the Great Basin—a lower area containing smaller ranges and low-lying deserts—in between. The highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Denali" title="Denali">Denali</a> in Alaska.</p>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120722022527/http://egsc.usgs.gov/isb/pubs/booklets/elvadist/elvadist.html" rel="nofollow">United States Geographical Survey (USGS)</a> states that the geographic center of North America is "6 miles [10 km] west of <a href="/wiki/Balta,_North_Dakota" title="Balta, North Dakota">Balta, Pierce County, North Dakota</a>" at about <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=North_America&amp;params=48_10_N_100_10_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">48°10′N</span> <span class="longitude">100°10′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">48.167°N 100.167°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">48.167; -100.167</span></span></span></a></span>, about 24 kilometres (15 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Rugby,_North_Dakota" title="Rugby, North Dakota">Rugby, North Dakota</a>. The USGS further states that "No marked or monumented point has been established by any government agency as the geographic center of either the 50 States, the conterminous United States, or the North American continent." Nonetheless, there is a 4.6-metre (15 ft) field stone <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisk</a> in Rugby claiming to mark the center. The North American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_pole_of_inaccessibility" title="Continental pole of inaccessibility">continental pole of inaccessibility</a> is located 1,650 km (1,030 mi) from the nearest coastline, between <a href="/wiki/Allen,_South_Dakota" title="Allen, South Dakota">Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyle,_South_Dakota" title="Kyle, South Dakota">Kyle</a>, South Dakota at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=North_America&amp;params=43.36_N_101.97_W_&amp;title=Pole+of+Inaccessibility+North+America"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">43°22′N</span> <span class="longitude">101°58′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">43.36°N 101.97°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">43.36; -101.97</span></span><span style="display:none">﻿ (<span class="fn org">Pole of Inaccessibility North America</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PIA_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-PIA-67">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="16122" data-file-width="10347" height="343" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg/220px-Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg/330px-Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg/440px-Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geologic_map_of_North_America.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geologic map of North America</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_america_rock_types.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2146" data-file-width="644" height="500" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/North_america_rock_types.jpg/150px-North_america_rock_types.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/North_america_rock_types.jpg/225px-North_america_rock_types.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/North_america_rock_types.jpg/300px-North_america_rock_types.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_North_America" title="Geology of North America">Geology of North America</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_geology">Canadian geology</span></h4>
<p>Geologically, Canada is one of the oldest regions in the world, with more than half of the region consisting of <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">precambrian</a> rocks that have been above sea level since the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeozoic" title="Palaeozoic">Palaeozoic</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marianopolis_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marianopolis-68">[61]</a></sup> Canada's mineral resources are diverse and extensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marianopolis_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marianopolis-68">[61]</a></sup> Across the Canadian Shield and in the north there are large iron, nickel, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, copper, gold, lead, <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> reserves. Large diamond concentrations have been recently developed in the Arctic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[62]</a></sup> making Canada one of the world's largest producers. Throughout the Shield there are many mining towns extracting these minerals. The largest, and best known, is <a href="/wiki/Greater_Sudbury" title="Greater Sudbury">Sudbury</a>, Ontario. Sudbury is an exception to the normal process of forming minerals in the Shield since there is significant evidence that the <a href="/wiki/Sudbury_Basin" title="Sudbury Basin">Sudbury Basin</a> is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">meteorite</a> <a href="/wiki/Impact_crater" title="Impact crater">impact crater</a>. The nearby, but less known <a href="/wiki/Temagami_Magnetic_Anomaly" title="Temagami Magnetic Anomaly">Temagami Magnetic Anomaly</a> has striking similarities to the Sudbury Basin. Its magnetic anomalies are very similar to the Sudbury Basin, and so it could be a second metal-rich impact crater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GH_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-GH-70">[63]</a></sup> The Shield is also covered by vast boreal forests that support an important logging industry.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="US_geological_provinces">US geological provinces</span></h4>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">lower 48 US states</a> can be divided into roughly five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physiography" title="Physiography">physiographic</a> provinces:</p>
<ol>
<li>The American cordillera.</li>
<li>The Canadian Shield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marianopolis_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-Marianopolis-68">[61]</a></sup> Northern portion of the upper midwestern United States.</li>
<li>The stable platform.</li>
<li>The coastal plain.</li>
<li>The Appalachian <a href="/wiki/Orogeny" title="Orogeny">orogenic</a> belt.</li>
</ol>
<p>The geology of Alaska is typical of that of the cordillera, while the major islands of Hawaii consist of <a href="/wiki/Neogene" title="Neogene">Neogene</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanics</a> erupted over a <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(geology)" title="Hotspot (geology)">hot spot</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2938" data-file-width="3300" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg/180px-North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg/270px-North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg/360px-North_america_terrain_2003_map.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">North America <a href="/wiki/Bedrock" title="Bedrock">bedrock</a> and terrain</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_america_basement_rocks.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="484" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/North_america_basement_rocks.png/180px-North_america_basement_rocks.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/North_america_basement_rocks.png/270px-North_america_basement_rocks.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/North_america_basement_rocks.png/360px-North_america_basement_rocks.png 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">North American <a href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">cratons</a> and basement rocks</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_American_geology">Central American geology</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/220px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/330px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/440px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FAD4AF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Central America rests in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Central America is geologically active with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruption" title="Volcanic eruption">volcanic eruptions</a> and earthquakes occurring from time to time. In 1976 Guatemala was hit by a <a href="/wiki/1976_Guatemala_earthquake" title="1976 Guatemala earthquake">major earthquake</a>, killing 23,000 people; Managua, the capital of Nicaragua, was devastated by earthquakes in 1931 and 1972, the last one killing about 5,000 people; three earthquakes devastated El Salvador, one in 1986 and two in 2001; one <a href="/wiki/2009_Costa_Rica_earthquake" title="2009 Costa Rica earthquake">earthquake</a> devastated northern and central Costa Rica in 2009, killing at least 34 people; in <a href="/wiki/2009_Honduras_earthquake" title="2009 Honduras earthquake">Honduras</a> a powerful earthquake killed seven people in 2009.</p>
<p>Volcanic eruptions are common in the region. In 1968 the <a href="/wiki/Arenal_Volcano" title="Arenal Volcano">Arenal Volcano</a>, in Costa Rica, erupted and killed 87 people. Fertile soils from weathered volcanic lavas have made it possible to sustain dense populations in the agriculturally productive highland areas.</p>
<p>Central America has many <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain ranges</a>; the longest are the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">Sierra Madre de Chiapas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Isabelia" title="Cordillera Isabelia">Cordillera Isabelia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_Talamanca" title="Cordillera de Talamanca">Cordillera de Talamanca</a>. Between the mountain ranges lie fertile valleys that are suitable for the people; in fact, most of the population of Honduras, Costa Rica, and Guatemala live in valleys. Valleys are also suitable for the production of coffee, beans, and other crops.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1425" data-file-width="1900" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North_America_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
North America map of Köppen climate classification.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North America is a very large continent which surpasses the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>. Greenland, along with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_shield" title="Canadian shield">Canadian shield</a>, is tundra with average temperatures ranging from between 10 to 20 °C (50 to 68 °F), but central Greenland is composed of a very large ice sheet. This tundra radiates throughout Canada, but its border ends near the Rocky Mountains (but still contains Alaska) and at the end of the Canadian Shield, near the Great Lakes. Climate west of the Cascades is described as being a temperate weather with average precipitation 20 inches (510 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[64]</a></sup> Climate in coastal California is described to be Mediterranean, with average temperatures in cities like San Francisco ranging from between 57 to 70 °F (14 to 21 °C) over the course of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Stretching from the East Coast to eastern North Dakota, and stretching down to Kansas, is the continental-humid climate featuring hard seasons, with a large amount of annual precipitation, with places like New York City averaging 50 inches (1,300 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[66]</a></sup> Starting at the southern border of the continental-humid climate and stretching to the Gulf of Mexico (whilst encompassing the eastern half of Texas) is the subtropical climate. This area has the wettest cities in the contiguous U.S. with annual precipitation reaching 67 inches (1,700 mm) in Mobile, Alabama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[67]</a></sup> Stretching from the borders of the continental humid and subtropical climates, and going west to the Cascades Sierra Nevada, south to the southern tip of durango, north to the border with tundra climate, the steppe/desert climate is the driest climate in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">

</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_States" title="Demographics of the United States">Demographics of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Canada" title="Demographics of Canada">Demographics of Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mexico" title="Demographics of Mexico">Demographics of Mexico</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="783" data-file-width="700" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif/220px-Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif/330px-Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif/440px-Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Non-Native_American_Nations_Control_over_N_America_1750-2008.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Non-native nations' control and claims over North America c. 1750–2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="691" data-file-width="624" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG/220px-Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG/330px-Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG/440px-Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_Americas.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Languages spoken in the Americas</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Langs_N.Amer.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="1290" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/220px-Langs_N.Amer.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/330px-Langs_N.Amer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Langs_N.Amer.png/440px-Langs_N.Amer.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Langs_N.Amer.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">Native languages</a> of the US, Canada and Greenland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Economically, Canada and the United States are the wealthiest and most <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed nations</a> in the continent, followed by Mexico, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_countries" title="Newly industrialized countries">newly industrialized country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIA_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-76">[69]</a></sup> The countries of Central America and the Caribbean are at various levels of economic and human development. For example, small Caribbean island-nations, such as Barbados, Trinidad and Tobago, and Antigua and Barbuda, have a higher <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> than Mexico due to their smaller populations. Panama and Costa Rica have a significantly higher <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> and GDP than the rest of the Central American nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-77">[70]</a></sup> Additionally, despite Greenland's vast resources in oil and minerals, much of them remain untapped, and the island is economically dependent on fishing, tourism, and subsidies from Denmark. Nevertheless, the island is highly developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Demographically, North America is ethnically diverse. Its three main groups are <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_race" title="Caucasian race">Caucasians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Blacks</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There is a significant minority of Indigenous Americans and <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a> among other less numerous groups.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">Languages of North America</a></div>
<p>The dominant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages_in_North_America" title="Languages in North America">languages in North America</a> are English, Spanish, and French. Danish is prevalent in Greenland alongside <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a>, and Dutch is spoken side by side local languages in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Dutch Caribbean</a>. The term Anglo-America is used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">anglophone</a> countries of the Americas: namely Canada (where English and French are co-official) and the United States, but also sometimes Belize and parts of the tropics, especially the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Caribbean" title="Commonwealth Caribbean">Commonwealth Caribbean</a>. Latin America refers to the other areas of the Americas (generally south of the United States) where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">Romance languages</a>, derived from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>, of Spanish and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> (but French speaking countries are not usually included) predominate: the other republics of Central America (but not always Belize), part of the Caribbean (not the Dutch-, English-, or French-speaking areas), Mexico, and most of South America (except <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> (France), and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> (UK)).</p>
<p>The French language has historically played a significant role in North America and now retains a distinctive presence in some regions. Canada is officially bilingual. French is the official language of the Province of Quebec, where 95% of the people speak it as either their first or second language, and it is co-official with English in the Province of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>. Other French-speaking locales include the Province of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> (the official language is English, but there are an estimated 600,000 Franco-Ontarians), the Province of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> (co-official as <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> with English), the <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre_et_Miquelon" title="Saint-Pierre et Miquelon">Saint-Pierre et Miquelon</a>, as well as the US state of Louisiana, where French is also an official language. Haiti is included with this group based on historical association but Haitians speak both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" title="Haitian Creole language">Creole</a> and French. Similarly, French and French Antillean Creole is spoken in Saint Lucia and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Dominica" title="Commonwealth of Dominica">Commonwealth of Dominica</a> alongside English.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_North_America" title="Religion in North America">Religion in North America</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religions_of_the_world" title="Religions of the world">Religions of the world</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6515" data-file-width="5167" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg/170px-WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg/255px-WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg/340px-WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WashingtonNationalCathedralHighsmith15393v.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Washington_National_Cathedral" title="Washington National Cathedral">Washington National Cathedral</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>. The United States has the largest Christian population in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the largest religion in the United States, Canada and Mexico according to a 2012 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> survey, 77.4% of the population considered themselves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[72]</a></sup> Christianity also is the predominant religion <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_North_America" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America">in the 23 dependent territories in North America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[73]</a></sup> The United States has the <a href="/wiki/Christianity_by_country" title="Christianity by country">largest Christian population</a> in the world, with nearly 247 million Christians (70%), although other countries have higher percentages of Christians among their populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[74]</a></sup> Mexico has the world's second largest number of Catholics, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the same study <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">religiously unaffiliated</a> (include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agnostic" title="Agnostic">agnostic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist">atheist</a>) make up about 17.1% of the population of Canada and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religiously_Unaffiliated_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Religiously_Unaffiliated-83">[76]</a></sup> No religion make up about 22.8% of the United States population, and 23.9% of Canada total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2011_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-religion2011-84">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canada, the United States and Mexico host communities of both <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (6 million or about 1.8%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[78]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a> (3.8 million or 1.1%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[79]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> (3.4 million or 1.0%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[80]</a></sup> The biggest number of Jewish individuals can be found in the United States (5.4 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[81]</a></sup> Canada (375,000)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[82]</a></sup> and Mexico (67,476).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEGI_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI-90">[83]</a></sup> The United States host the largest Muslim population in North America with 2.7 million or 0.9%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew2015_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew2015-91">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam_in_the_United_States_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_in_the_United_States-92">[85]</a></sup> While Canada host about one million Muslim or 3.2% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[86]</a></sup> While in Mexico there were 3,700 Muslims in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010-census_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-94">[87]</a></sup> In 2012, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-T_San_Diego" title="U-T San Diego">U-T San Diego</a></i> estimated U.S. practitioners of Buddhism at 1.2 million people, of whom 40% are living in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The predominant religion in Central America is Christianity (95.6%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context-96">[89]</a></sup> Beginning with the Spanish colonization of Central America in the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> became the most popular religion in the region until the first half of the 20th century. Since the 1960s, there has been an increase in other Christian groups, particularly <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, as well as other religious organizations, and individuals identifying themselves as having no religion. Also Christianity is the predominant religion in the Caribbean (84.7%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Christianity_in_its_Global_Context-96">[89]</a></sup> Other religious groups in the region are <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafari</a> (in Jamaica), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-American_religions" title="Afro-American religions">Afro-American religions</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">Santería</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Vodou</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Populace">Populace</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:left/right/center;background-color:">North American cities</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
